  372. Gillette made a huge mistake marketing heavily on the Mach 3 in the late 90's over the competitors two blade technology. It has stuck ever since to a significant proportion of men (local and abroad) and in many respects, their children who grew up with influencers to the product whom to a great extent, refuse to upgrade.<br /><br />Like ink jet printers, these shavers are being sold cheap in anticipation of recovering costs from the blade cartridges. The Fusion Proglide line manages to be even more expensive over previous generations which makes little justification for those who find no issues with their current 3/4/5 blade shaver. To stop producing previous generation blades would cause an uproar.<br /><br />Subsequent four and five blades meant that the shave head ended up to be 'larger' and less 'precise control' over the Mach 3. The marketing worked briefly - more blades surely has got to be 'better' but not all consumers are fools to give in which is why Mach 3 still exists after a decade, the Flexball seems like a last attempt to revive the market and in many respects is still largely a 'gimmick' as many have mentioned.<br /><br />However where attributes do differ is the Proglide blades are definitely thinner over the Fusion ones and has improved the shaving experience with less resistance and comparable to the experience of using the Mach 3 for the first time. I struggled to find justification for the Flexball for several weeks as the wrist movements often cancel out the requirement for the blade to 'flex' around the face - to the point I admitted to myself that it was just a marketing tactic and a waste of money.<br /><br />I then realised that this shaver is also suited for other 'areas' of the body other than the face (whether Gillette will readily admit/endorse or otherwise). The Flexball definitely will assist in shaving more difficult and challenging to reach parts of the body and if you do like to keep things groomed (even down there) this will offer a slight improvement through better control due to the flexing blade head.<br /><br />Lastly, this model is slightly larger than previous generation models so take this into account if you do travel; and if you are going to attempt to experiment with grooming areas other than your face, do use a different blade cartridge.etter control due to the flexing blade head. I spent a little more than that for my straight razor and accessories a couple of years ago and haven't bought anything since (except for shave soaps and such.) I think I will stick with the straight razor, I just like the shave better and my cost over time is less.back.<br /><br />All in all, this razor is well made and does a good job.   496. First a little background on my typical shaving routine, so you know where I'm coming from. I have sensitive skin and my facial hair grows slowly. I can typically get away with shaving 1-2 days per week without getting overly scruffy. A single pass was sufficient to remove almost all hair, with a few short touch-up strokes required to get those odd areas like right below the nose, and around the curves of my chin, which I expected. The glide is smooth. I've shaved about half a dozen times with this razor and the included blade is still working well. I expect that it will need to be replaced after a few more shaves.<br /><br />This razor includes a &#34;Flexball&#34; which allows the head of the razor to pivot side to side. It's explained on the package that this is supposed to lead to a more comfortable shave as it allows the razor to respond to the contours of your face to &#34;get virtually every hair&#34;. While shaving I tried to pay special attention to watching the razor's head in the mirror to see if it actually helped or not. From what I could tell, the Flexball appeared to have minimal advantage. The head of the razor did not appear to move very often at all, so I'm not sure it was really doing anything. In practice, my shave seemed to take just as long as usual. As I explained above I still needed to go back and touch up certain areas, which is something Gillette claims the Flexball should eliminate. As it stands, the Flexball seems do offer little advantage, and comes across as a marketing gimmick to entice consumers into &#34;upgrading&#34; the handle of their razor from the standard-issue Gillette Fusion. It's worth noting that all Gillette Fusion razors (regular, powered, Flexball, etc) all use the same razor cartridges. If you already have an existing Fusion razor, I don't see any advantage in &#34;upgrading&#34; to one with the Flexball. But if your current handle is old and busted, this would be a find replacement.<br /><br />Before using the Fusion Proglide with Flexball razor, I had been using a Schick Hydro-5. At the end of the day, I did not notice any major difference in my shave between the Schick and Gillette razors. Both do a great job. However, I do prefer the hydration strip on the Schick razors over the Gillette ones, especially the Hydro-5 as it has the added ability to flip-back the hydration strip to get it out of the way, making it easier to shave those hard to reach spots. But even without those added benefits, I would continue to stick with the Schick as I don't feel like the Gillette products warrant their markedly higher retail costs.<br /><br />Note: I received this product directly from the brand.Fusion razor, I don't see any advantage in &#34;upgrading&#34; to one with the Flexball. The razor is very hefty--about 1.8 oz measured on my scale. By contrast, a disposable typically weighs-in less than 1 oz. I measured a Gillette disposable at 1/2 oz.<br /><br />▲ The razor body is very solid, and has a comfortable feel to it. I liked the feel of the razor body--it felt solidly constructed, and is also well-balanced. I also liked the black raised ergonomic contours on the body of the razor. Again--felt very solid and well constructed. The color of the body is black with silver trim, plus the orange Flexball.<br /><br />▲ For &#34;Field Test #1,&#34; I did not shave for several days, so that I had a 3-day beard. I washed my face with cool water, left my face wet, then applied a smooth layer of the Proglide gel. I then waited several minutes for my beard to soften. I began shaving in the easier portions of my face, where the whiskers are lighter, then proceeded to the heavier sections around my chin. The razor nicely navigated all the crags and contours without the slightest drag or snagging. The blades cut very close without the hint of scraping or cutting. I examined my face very closely after shaving, and I was very pleased with the result. The razor did an outstanding job, providing a very close, clean shave. (For the records, I do NOT have a really smooth face--it's about normal roughness.)<br /><br />▲ For &#34;Field Test #2,&#34; I had just the normal 1-day beard. I washed my face with warm water, left my face wet, then similarly applied a layer of the same gel. I waited exactly 3 1/2 minutes for the bristles to soften. This time, I paid attention to how well the razor traversed over the chin and down to the neck. I wanted to see if the rotating head of the razor could smoothly navigate this hilly territory. As before the razor did a similarly outstanding job, providing a very close and smooth shave. Thus, both the Field Tests confirm the capability of this product. It works as advertised. When I completed my shaving, I rinsed the razor, and noticed that it is somewhat difficult to get the blades entirely clean of shaving gel. With 5 blades closely spaced together, this is not a trivial feat. After cleaning, I thoroughly dried the cartridge, as I hope to extend the life of the blades.<br /><br />▲ The famous &#34;Flexball&#34; is obvious because of its bright orange color. The Flexball pivots in 2 different ways. As you hold the razor in front of you, it pivots left to right, in an angular fashion--perhaps up to 15 degrees in each direction. There are little &#34;stops&#34; on the Flexball that prevent it from rotating too far. You can see a very fine band (at first I thought it was a wire) that allows the angular pivoting. This movement is very smooth--no hitches whatsoever. There is a small screw-like pivot-point, around which the movement takes place. This fastener appears to be very solid; I doubt anything will come lose. The head of the razor also pivots forward and back, using a thin &#34;bar&#34; going into the head of the razor.<br /><br />▲ The above Flexball is very impressive engineering. It appears to operate flawlessly. All of this is to allow the razor to match the contours of your face. That's a nice way of saying, shave around all those divots and dents in your face (not that YOU have any, of course, but someone else might.) To further get around those slight detours, this product uses extremely thin, five blades that are designed to glide more smoothly; thus, there is no tugging on your skin.<br /><br />▲ Gillette also claims to incorporate a proprietary strip called the &#34;Enhanced Lubrastrip.&#34; It's the part of the cartridge that is pale green. This strip contains mineral oil and &#34;lubricating polymers.&#34; Well, my skin appreciated those &#34;polymers.&#34;<br /><br />✔ SUMMARY: My shaving &#34;test&#34; passed with flying colors. My shave was very smooth, very close, no tugs, no snags. The razor feels very solid. One possible caveat--the razor itself, and the replacement blades are not cheap compared to other products. However, it seems unfair to lower the rating because of the cost; the shopper can make their own decision.<br /><br />Highly Recommend!<br /><br />♫ A Review by Chris LawsonY: My shaving &#34;test&#34; passed with flying colors. My shave was very smooth, very close, no tugs, no snags. The razor feels very solid. One possible caveat--the razor itself, and the replacement blades are not cheap compared to other products. However, it seems unfair to lower the rating because of the cost; the shopper can make their own decision.<br /><br />Highly Recommend!<br /><br />♫ A Review by Chris Lawson

  568. Having tried the Fusion line when it first released, I was anxious to try the new renditions after Gillette modified their blades (\\"ProGlide\\") and attached them to the nifty handle that rocks side-to-side in addition to front and back (\\"FlexBall handle technology\\").<br /><br />After loving the Mach 3 then hating the original Fusion as I moved on to new shaving technology, I've wound up as a self-proclaimed Schick Quattro fanboy. I haven't been able to find a razor that offers a shave even close in comfort, but as most men, I'm never satisfied. As such, I gave the new \\"Fusion ProFlide Razor with FlexBall handle technology\\" every chance in the world to impress.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the new Fusion with all its bells and whistles is no better than the original. How, specifically? It all has to do with the shave (obviously, I suppose). It yields an extremely uncomfortable pulling sensation, even when shaving with the grain. I didn't try shaving against it, as it would've been extremely painful.<br /><br />What I was left with was a shave that left noticeable stubble and an obvious case of razor burn; this is with a brand new set of blades! It's hard to tell what I'd have after a week's use. This is simply unacceptable for blades that are so spendy.<br /><br />So what about that fancy \\"FlexBall\\" handle? A gimmick. I suppose if your wrists and fingers can't bend at all it might be something that you'd enjoy, but I honestly can't tell the difference between it and a normal handle in actual use.<br /><br />So what does Gillette have wrong? As best I can tell from comparing the design with my Schick, it's very simple. Schick runs tiny wires perpendicular to the blades. Gillette does no such thing. It seems to me that the wires in the Schick prevent the blades from flexing and separating, and so they cut as a more cohesive unit. The Gillette blades flex very easily and as a result, pull apart and work much more like one of the old, single-bladed nightmares as opposed to a modern, advanced shaving instrument. The other added advantage of the Schick design is that it's nearly impossible to cut yourself. Not so with the Fusion.<br /><br />Gillette: you're better than this. This product doesn't even come close to providing the quality experience that the company purports to offer.<br /><br />Full disclosure: I received the \\"Fusion ProGlide Razor with FlexBall handle technology\\" to try from Gillette as part of their promotion for the new product, free of charge.as opposed to a modern, advanced shaving instrument.
